## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / nonlinear oscillators
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration (dv/dt) depends on velocity and time. The position variable is absent but may be implicitly represented through trigonometric functions of time or through integral relationships with velocity, leading to possible sinusoidal time dependence and nonlinear velocity-dependent damping/driving terms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear restoring (sinusoidal proxy): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t + c2) (simple harmonic oscillator with position replaced by sinusoidal time dependence)
- Linear damping: dv_dt = c0 * v (linear velocity-dependent damping/driving)
- Cubic velocity nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 (nonlinear damping term as in Rayleigh oscillator)
- Van der Pol form: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (nonlinear damping plus implicit restoring force)
- Quadratic velocity: dv_dt = c0 * v**2 + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (quadratic drag with restoring force)
- Duffing-like driven: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t) + c2 * sin(c1 * t)**3 + c3 * v (cubic restoring force with x ~ sin(Žēt))
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * v * (c1 + c2 * v**2) + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (velocity-dependent nonlinear damping with restoring)
- Mixed nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * v * sin(c1 * t) + c2 * cos(c1 * t) (coupling between velocity and time-periodic terms)
- Polynomial velocity with harmonic drive: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t) + c2 * v + c3 * v**2 + c4 * v**3 (general nonlinear oscillator expansion)
- Mathieu-type parametric: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (parametric excitation)
- Limit cycle form: dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - v**2) * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (Van der Pol style limit cycle with restoring)
- Velocity-position coupling proxy: dv_dt = c0 * cos(c1 * t) * v + c2 * sin(c1 * t) (x┬Ęv type coupling with x ~ sin(Žēt))

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Nonlinear damping in oscillators ŌåÆ odd-power velocity terms (v┬│, vŌüĄ) that preserve time-reversal symmetry breaking
- Implicit position dependence ŌåÆ sinusoidal functions of time sin(c*t), cos(c*t) serve as proxies for displacement in periodic systems
- Self-sustained oscillations (limit cycles) ŌåÆ terms of the form (1 - v┬▓)*v indicating amplitude-dependent energy balance
- Parametric resonance ŌåÆ products of periodic time functions with velocity, e.g., cos(c*t)*v
- Phase-space structure preservation ŌåÆ acceleration terms that are odd functions of velocity for symmetric oscillators
- Frequency mixing in nonlinear oscillators ŌåÆ products of trigonometric functions at different frequencies or harmonics
- Energy-based formulation ŌåÆ acceleration expressible as gradient of effective potential plus dissipation: dv/dt = -dU/dx + Q(v)
- Autonomous vs driven decomposition ŌåÆ separate velocity-only terms (autonomous dynamics) from explicit time-dependent terms (external forcing)
